<p><b>Siri</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɪr/: &#39;irr&#39; in &#39;mirror&#39;">ɪr</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/2\/22\/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Flame%2C_not_lame-Siri.wav\/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Flame%2C_not_lame-Siri.wav.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;LL-Q1860 (eng)-Flame, not lame-Siri.wav&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/22/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Flame%2C_not_lame-Siri.wav/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Flame%2C_not_lame-Siri.wav.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:LL-Q1860_(eng)-Flame,_not_lame-Siri.wav" title="File:LL-Q1860 (eng)-Flame, not lame-Siri.wav">ⓘ</a></sup></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">SEER</span>-ee</i></a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Virtual_assistant" title="Virtual assistant">virtual assistant</a> and chatbot purchased, developed, and popularized by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, which is included in the <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPadOS" title="IPadOS">iPadOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/WatchOS" title="WatchOS">watchOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV_(device)" title="Apple TV (device)">Apple TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/AudioOS" class="mw-redirect" title="AudioOS">audioOS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/VisionOS" title="VisionOS">visionOS</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It uses voice queries, gesture based control, focus-tracking and a <a href="/wiki/Natural-language_user_interface" title="Natural-language user interface">natural-language user interface</a> to answer questions, make recommendations, and perform actions by delegating requests to a set of <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> services. With continued use, it adapts to users' individual language usages, searches, and preferences, returning individualized results.
</p><p>Siri is a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spin-off</a> from a project developed by the <a href="/wiki/SRI_International" title="SRI International">SRI International</a> Artificial Intelligence Center. Its <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">speech recognition</a> engine was provided by <a href="/wiki/Nuance_Communications" title="Nuance Communications">Nuance Communications</a>, and it uses advanced <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a> technologies to function. Its original American, British, and Australian <a href="/wiki/Voice_acting" title="Voice acting">voice actors</a> recorded their respective voices around 2005, unaware of the recordings' eventual usage. Siri was released as an app for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> in February 2010. Two months later, Apple acquired it and integrated it into the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4s" title="IPhone 4s">iPhone 4s</a> at its release on 4 October 2011, removing the separate app from the iOS <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" class="mw-redirect" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a>. Siri has since been an integral part of Apple's products, having been adapted into other hardware devices including newer <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> models, <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macintosh" class="mw-redirect" title="Macintosh">Mac</a>, <a href="/wiki/AirPods" title="AirPods">AirPods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV_(device)" title="Apple TV (device)">Apple TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/HomePod" title="HomePod">HomePod</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Vision_Pro" title="Apple Vision Pro">Apple Vision Pro</a>.
</p><p>Siri supports a wide range of user commands, including performing phone actions, checking basic information, scheduling events and reminders, handling device settings, searching the Internet, navigating areas, finding information on entertainment, and being able to engage with iOS-integrated apps. With the release of <a href="/wiki/IOS_10" title="IOS 10">iOS 10</a>, in 2016, Apple opened up limited third-party access to Siri, including third-party messaging apps, as well as payments, <a href="/wiki/Ride-sharing" class="mw-redirect" title="Ride-sharing">ride-sharing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Voice_over_IP" title="Voice over IP">Internet calling</a> apps. With the release of <a href="/wiki/IOS_11" title="IOS 11">iOS 11</a>, Apple updated Siri's voice and added support for follow-up questions, language translation, and additional third-party actions.
<a href="/wiki/IOS_17" title="IOS 17">iOS 17</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPadOS_17" title="IPadOS 17">iPadOS 17</a> enabled users to activate Siri by simply saying "Siri", while the previous command, "Hey Siri", is still supported. 
</p><p>In 2024, Apple added initial <a href="/wiki/Large_language_model" title="Large language model">large-language-model</a> functionality to Siri in <a href="/wiki/IOS_18" title="IOS 18">iOS 18</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPadOS_18" title="IPadOS 18">iPadOS 18</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MacOS_Sequoia" title="MacOS Sequoia">macOS Sequoia</a>, including <a href="/wiki/ChatGPT" title="ChatGPT">ChatGPT</a> integration. In 2025, Apple announced that a broader overhaul of Siri based on <a href="/wiki/Apple_Intelligence" title="Apple Intelligence">Apple Intelligence</a>, intended to enable increased personalization, would be delayed due to technical challenges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2026, they released MacOS Tahoe, which also came with Siri support.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Development">Development</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Siri is a <a href="/wiki/Spin-out" class="mw-redirect" title="Spin-out">spin-out</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Research_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanford Research Institute">Stanford Research Institute</a>'s Artificial Intelligence Center and is an offshoot of the US <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency</a>'s (DARPA)-funded <a href="/wiki/CALO" title="CALO">CALO</a> project.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-HuffPost&#95;origins&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HuffPost_origins-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SRI_International" title="SRI International">SRI International</a> used the NABC Framework to define the value proposition for Siri.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was co-founded by Dag Kittlaus, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Gruber" title="Tom Gruber">Tom Gruber</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Cheyer" title="Adam Cheyer">Adam Cheyer</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-HuffPost&#95;origins&#95;4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HuffPost_origins-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kittlaus named Siri after a co-worker in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>; <a href="/wiki/Siri_(given_name)" title="Siri (given name)">the name</a> is a short form of the name <a href="/wiki/Sigrid" title="Sigrid">Sigrid</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Norse language">Old Norse</a> <i>Sigríðr</i>, composed of the elements <i>sigr</i> "victory" and <i>fríðr</i> "beautiful".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Siri's <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">speech recognition</a> engine was provided by <a href="/wiki/Nuance_Communications" title="Nuance Communications">Nuance Communications</a>, a speech technology company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nuance&#95;confirmed&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuance_confirmed-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Neither Apple nor Nuance acknowledged this for years,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> until Nuance CEO Paul Ricci confirmed it at a 2013 technology conference.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nuance&#95;confirmed&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuance_confirmed-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The speech recognition system uses sophisticated <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a> techniques, including <a href="/wiki/Convolutional_neural_network" title="Convolutional neural network">convolutional neural networks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_short-term_memory" title="Long short-term memory">long short-term memory</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The initial Siri prototype was implemented using the Active platform, a joint project between the Artificial Intelligence Center of <a href="/wiki/SRI_International" title="SRI International">SRI International</a> and the Vrai Group at <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Polytechnique_F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_de_Lausanne" title="École Polytechnique Fédérale de Lausanne">École Polytechnique Fédérale de Lausanne</a>. The Active platform was the focus of a Ph.D. thesis led by <a href="/wiki/Didier_Guzzoni" title="Didier Guzzoni">Didier Guzzoni</a>, who joined Siri as its chief scientist.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Siri was acquired by Apple Inc. in April 2010 under the direction of Steve Jobs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apple's first notion of a digital personal assistant appeared in a 1987 concept video, <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Navigator" title="Knowledge Navigator">Knowledge Navigator</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Siri's original release on iPhone 4s in October 2011 received mixed reviews. It received praise for its <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">voice recognition</a> and contextual knowledge of user information, including calendar appointments, but was criticized for requiring stiff user commands and having a lack of flexibility. It was also criticized for lacking information on certain nearby places and for its inability to understand certain <a href="/wiki/English_accents" class="mw-redirect" title="English accents">English accents</a>. During the mid-2010s, a number of media reports said that Siri lacked innovation, particularly against new competing voice assistants. The reports concerned Siri's limited set of features, "bad" voice recognition, and undeveloped service integrations as causing trouble for Apple in the field of <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> and cloud-based services; the basis for the complaints reportedly due to stifled development, as caused by Apple's prioritization of user <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">privacy</a> and executive power struggles within the company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WSJ&#95;innovation&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_innovation-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its launch was also overshadowed by the death of <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a>, which occurred one day after the launch.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Apple_Intelligence">Apple Intelligence</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Apple Intelligence"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_Intelligence" title="Apple Intelligence">Apple Intelligence</a></div>
<p>Siri has been updated with enhanced capabilities made possible by Apple Intelligence. In <a href="/wiki/MacOS_Sequoia" title="MacOS Sequoia">macOS Sequoia</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS_18" title="IOS 18">iOS 18</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IPadOS_18" title="IPadOS 18">iPadOS 18</a>, Siri features an updated user interface, improved <a href="/wiki/Natural_language_processing" title="Natural language processing">natural language processing</a>, and the option to interact via text by double tapping the home bar without enabling the feature in the Accessibility menu on iOS and iPadOS. According to Apple: it adds the ability for Siri to use the context of device activities to make conversations more natural; Siri can give users device support and will have larger app support via the Siri App Intents API; Siri will be able to deliver intelligence that's tailored to the user and their on-device information using personal context. For example, a user can say, "When is Mom's flight landing?" and Siri will find the flight details and try to cross-reference them with real-time flight tracking to give an arrival time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For more day to day interactions with <a href="/wiki/List_of_Apple_products" title="List of Apple products">Apple devices</a>, Siri will now summarize messages (on more apps than just Messages, such as Discord and Slack). According to users<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2025)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, this feature can be helpful but can also be inappropriate in certain situations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2026, Apple announced that it has selected Google Gemini to "power AI features like Siri".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Voices">Voices</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Voices"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The original American voice of Siri was recorded in July 2005 by <a href="/wiki/Susan_Bennett" title="Susan Bennett">Susan Bennett</a>, who was unaware it would eventually be used for the voice assistant.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-McKee&#95;2017&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKee_2017-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Original&#95;voice&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Original_voice-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A report from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Verge" title="The Verge">The Verge</a></i> in September 2013 about voice actors, their work, and machine learning developments, hinted that Allison Dufty was the voice behind Siri,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but this was disproven when Dufty wrote on her website that she was "absolutely, positively <i>not</i> the voice of Siri."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Original&#95;voice&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Original_voice-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Citing growing pressure, Bennett revealed her role as Siri in October, and her claim was confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Edward_John_Primeau" title="Edward John Primeau">Ed Primeau</a>, an American <a href="/wiki/Audio_forensics" title="Audio forensics">audio forensics</a> expert.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Original&#95;voice&#95;21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Original_voice-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apple has never acknowledged it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Original&#95;voice&#95;21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Original_voice-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The original British male voice was provided by <a href="/wiki/Jon_Briggs" title="Jon Briggs">Jon Briggs</a>, a former technology journalist and for 12 years narrated for the hit <a href="/wiki/British_Broadcasting_Company" title="British Broadcasting Company">BBC</a> quiz show <a href="/wiki/The_Weakest_Link" class="mw-redirect" title="The Weakest Link">The Weakest Link</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-McKee&#95;2017&#95;20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKee_2017-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After discovering he was Siri's voice by watching television, he first spoke about the role in November 2011. He acknowledged that the voice work was done "five or six years ago", and that he didn't know how the recordings would be used.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The original Australian voice was provided by <a href="/wiki/Karen_Jacobsen" title="Karen Jacobsen">Karen Jacobsen</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Voice-over" title="Voice-over">voice-over</a> artist known in Australia as the <i><a href="/wiki/GPS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS">GPS</a> girl</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-McKee&#95;2017&#95;20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKee_2017-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Guardian&#95;voices&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_voices-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview between all three voice actors and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, Briggs said that "the original system was recorded for a US company called Scansoft, who were then bought by Nuance. Apple simply licensed it."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Guardian&#95;voices&#95;26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_voices-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For <a href="/wiki/IOS_11" title="IOS 11">iOS 11</a>, Apple auditioned hundreds of candidates to find new female voices, then recorded several hours of speech, including different personalities and expressions, to build a new <a href="/wiki/Speech_synthesis" title="Speech synthesis">text-to-speech</a> voice based on <a href="/wiki/Deep_learning" title="Deep learning">deep learning</a> technology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2022, Apple added Quinn, its first gender-neutral voice as a fifth user option, to the iOS 15.4 developer release.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Integration">Integration</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Integration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Siri released as a <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">stand-alone application</a> for the iOS operating system in February 2010, and at the time, the developers were also intending to release Siri for <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_OS" title="BlackBerry OS">BlackBerry</a> devices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two months later, Apple acquired Siri.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On October 4, 2011, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4S" class="mw-redirect" title="IPhone 4S">iPhone 4S</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Beta_version" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta version">beta version</a> of Siri.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After the announcement, Apple removed the existing standalone Siri app from <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" class="mw-redirect" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TechCrunch&#95;app&#95;removal&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TechCrunch_app_removal-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a></i> wrote that, though the Siri app supports <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4" title="IPhone 4">iPhone 4</a>, its removal from App Store might also have had a financial aspect for the company, in providing an incentive for customers to upgrade devices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TechCrunch&#95;app&#95;removal&#95;35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TechCrunch_app_removal-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Third-party developer Steven Troughton-Smith, however, managed to <a href="/wiki/Porting" title="Porting">port</a> Siri to iPhone 4, though without being able to communicate with Apple's servers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A few days later, Troughton-Smith, working with an anonymous person nicknamed "Chpwn", managed to fully hack Siri, enabling its full functionalities on iPhone 4 and <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a> devices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, developers were also able to successfully create and distribute legal ports of Siri to any device capable of running iOS 5, though a <a href="/wiki/Proxy_server" title="Proxy server">proxy server</a> was required for Apple server interaction.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_tv_gen_4_remote.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Apple_tv_gen_4_remote.jpeg/250px-Apple_tv_gen_4_remote.jpeg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Apple_tv_gen_4_remote.jpeg/500px-Apple_tv_gen_4_remote.jpeg 1.5x" data-file-width="3678" data-file-height="2451" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Siri_Remote" title="Siri Remote">Siri Remote</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV_(device)" title="Apple TV (device)">Apple TV</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Over the years, Apple has expanded the line of officially supported products, including newer iPhone models,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as well as iPad support in June 2012,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> iPod Touch support in September 2012,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apple TV support, and the stand-alone <a href="/wiki/Siri_Remote" title="Siri Remote">Siri Remote</a>, in September 2015,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Mac and AirPods support in September 2016,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and HomePod support in February 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Third_party_devices">Third party devices</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Third party devices"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>At the 2021 <a href="/wiki/Worldwide_Developers_Conference" title="Worldwide Developers Conference">Worldwide Developers Conference</a>, Apple announced that it would make Siri voice integration available in third party devices. Devices must be on the same wireless network as a <a href="/wiki/HomePod" title="HomePod">HomePod</a> or <a href="/wiki/HomePod_Mini" title="HomePod Mini">HomePod Mini</a> to route requests.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Ecobee" title="Ecobee">Ecobee</a> SmartThermostat with Voice Control became the first third-party device with built-in Siri control.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2024, <a href="/wiki/Denon" title="Denon">Denon</a> added Siri control to select soundbars and smart speakers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Features_and_options">Features and options</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Features and options"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Apple offers a wide range of voice commands to interact with Siri, including, but not limited to:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Phone and text actions, such as "Call Sarah", "Read my new messages", "Set the timer for 10 minutes", and "Send email to mom"</li>
<li>Check basic information, including "What's the weather like today?" and "How many dollars are in a euro?"</li>
<li>Find basic facts, including "How many people live in France?" and "How tall is Mount Everest?".  Siri usually uses Wikipedia to answer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Schedule events and reminders, including "Schedule a meeting" and "Remind me to<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>..."</li>
<li>Handle device settings, such as "Take a picture", "Turn off <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a>", and "Increase the brightness"</li>
<li>Search the Internet, including "Define<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>...", "Find pictures of<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>...", and "Search <a href="/wiki/Twitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> for<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>..."</li>
<li>Navigation, including "Take me home", "What's the traffic like on the way home?", and "Find driving directions to<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>..."</li>
<li>Translate words and phrases from English to a few languages, such as "How do I say where is the nearest hotel in French?"</li>
<li>Entertainment, such as "What basketball games are on today?", "What are some movies playing near me?", and "What's the synopsis of<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>...?"</li>
<li>Engage with iOS-integrated apps, including "Pause <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a>" and "Like this song"</li>
<li>Handle payments through Apple Pay, such as "Apple Pay 25 dollars to Mike for concert tickets" or "Send 41 dollars to Ivana."</li>
<li>Share <a href="/wiki/Estimated_time_of_arrival" title="Estimated time of arrival">ETA</a> with others.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Jokes, "Hey Siri, knock knock."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Siri also offers numerous pre-programmed responses to amusing questions. Such questions include "What is the meaning of life?" to which Siri may reply "All evidence to date suggests it's chocolate"; "Why am I here?", to which it may reply "I don't know. Frankly, I've wondered that myself"; and "Will you marry me?", to which it may respond with "My <a href="/wiki/End-user_license_agreement" title="End-user license agreement">End User Licensing Agreement</a> does not cover <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a>. My apologies."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Initially limited to female voices for most countries where Siri was supported, Apple announced in June 2013 that Siri would feature a gender option, adding a male voice counterpart. Notable exceptions are the United Kingdom, France, and the Netherlands; those countries were first limited to male voices, then would later get female voice counterparts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, Apple added the ability for users to speak "Hey Siri" to summon the assistant without needing to hold the device.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2015, the "Hey Siri" feature was updated to include individualized voice recognition, a presumed effort to prevent non-owner activation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With the announcement of <a href="/wiki/IOS_10" title="IOS 10">iOS 10</a> in June 2016, Apple opened up limited third-party developer access to Siri through a dedicated <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interface">application programming interface</a> (API). The API restricts the usage of Siri to engaging with third-party messaging apps, payment apps, ride-sharing apps, and Internet calling apps.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In iOS 11, Siri is able to handle follow-up questions, supports language translation, and opens up to more third-party actions, including task management.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, users are able to type to Siri,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a new, privacy-minded "on-device learning" technique improves Siri's suggestions by privately analyzing personal usage of different iOS applications.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>iOS 17 and iPadOS 17 allows users to simply say "Siri" to initiate Siri, and the virtual assistant now supports back to back requests, allowing users to issue multiple requests and conversations without reactivating it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the public beta versions of iOS 17, iPadOS 17, and <a href="/wiki/MacOS_Sonoma" title="MacOS Sonoma">macOS Sonoma</a>, Apple added support for bilingual queries to Siri.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/IOS_18" title="IOS 18">iOS 18</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPadOS_18" title="IPadOS 18">iPadOS 18</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacOS_Sequoia" title="MacOS Sequoia">MacOS 15 Sequoia</a> brought <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, integrated with <a href="/wiki/ChatGPT" title="ChatGPT">ChatGPT</a>, to Siri.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apple calls this "<a href="/wiki/Apple_Intelligence" title="Apple Intelligence">Apple Intelligence</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Siri received mixed reviews during its beta release as an integrated part of the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4s" title="IPhone 4s">iPhone 4S</a> in October 2011.
</p><p>MG Siegler of <i><a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a></i> wrote that Siri was "great," understood much more, but had “no API that any developer can use“.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/David_Pogue" title="David Pogue">David Pogue</a> also praised Siri's <a href="/wiki/Natural_language_processing" title="Natural language processing">ability to understand context</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jacqui Cheng of <i><a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a></i> wrote that Apple's claims of what Siri could do were bold, and the early demos "even bolder", this was still in beta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cheng2011&#95;72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cheng2011-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>While praising its ability to "decipher our casual language" and deliver "very specific and accurate result," sometimes even providing additional information, Cheng noted and criticized its restrictions, particularly when the language moved away from "stiffer commands" into more human interactions. One example included the phrase "Send a text to Jason, Clint, Sam, and Lee saying we're having dinner at Silver Cloud," which Siri interpreted as sending a message to Jason only, containing the text "Clint Sam and Lee saying we're having dinner at Silver Cloud." She also noted a lack of proper editability.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cheng2011&#95;72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cheng2011-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s executive chairman and former chief, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schmidt" title="Eric Schmidt">Eric Schmidt</a>, conceded that Siri could pose a competitive threat to the company's core search business.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Siri was criticized by <a href="/wiki/Abortion-rights_movements" class="mw-redirect" title="Abortion-rights movements">pro-abortion rights organizations</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a> (ACLU) and <a href="/wiki/NARAL_Pro-Choice_America" class="mw-redirect" title="NARAL Pro-Choice America">NARAL Pro-Choice America</a>, after users found that Siri could not provide information about the location of birth control or abortion providers nearby, sometimes directing users to <a href="/wiki/Crisis_pregnancy_center" title="Crisis pregnancy center">crisis pregnancy centers</a> instead.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Natalie Kerris, a spokeswoman for Apple, told <i>The New York Times that, “</i>These are not intentional omissions…”.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In January 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Fast_Company_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fast Company (magazine)">Fast Company</a></i> reported that, in then-recent months, Siri had begun to confuse the word "abortion" with "<a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">adoption</a>", citing "health experts" who stated that the situation had "gotten worse." However, at the time of <i>Fast Company</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s report, the situation had changed slightly, with Siri offering "a more comprehensive list of <a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood" title="Planned Parenthood">Planned Parenthood</a> facilities", although "Adoption clinics continue to pop up, but near the bottom of the list."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Siri has also not been well received by some English speakers with distinctive accents, including <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scottish</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Americans from <a href="/wiki/Boston_accent" title="Boston accent">Boston</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Southern_American_English" title="Southern American English">South</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2012, Frank M. Fazio filed a class action lawsuit against Apple on behalf of the people who bought the iPhone 4S and felt misled about the capabilities of Siri, alleging its failure to function as depicted in Apple's Siri commercials. Fazio filed the lawsuit in California and claimed that the iPhone 4S was merely a "more expensive iPhone 4" if Siri fails to function as advertised.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On July 22, 2013, U.S. District Judge Claudia Wilken in San Francisco dismissed the suit but said the plaintiffs could amend at a later time. The reason given for dismissal was that plaintiffs did not sufficiently document enough misrepresentations by Apple for the trial to proceed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Perceived_lack_of_innovation">Perceived lack of innovation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Perceived lack of innovation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In June 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Verge" title="The Verge">The Verge</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Sean O'Kane wrote about the then-upcoming major iOS 10 updates, with a headline stating "Siri's big upgrades won't matter if it can't understand its users":
</p>
<blockquote><p>What Apple didn't talk about was solving Siri's biggest, most basic flaws: it's still not very good at voice recognition, and when it gets it right, the results are often clunky. And these problems look even worse when you consider that Apple now has full-fledged competitors in this space: <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Alexa" title="Amazon Alexa">Alexa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Cortana_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cortana (software)">Cortana</a>, and Google's <a href="/wiki/Google_Assistant" title="Google Assistant">Assistant</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote><p> Also writing for <i>The Verge</i>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Mossberg" title="Walt Mossberg">Walt Mossberg</a> had previously questioned Apple's efforts in cloud-based services, writing:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><blockquote><p>...<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>perhaps the biggest disappointment among Apple's cloud-based services is the one it needs most today, right now: Siri. Before Apple bought it, Siri was on the road to being a robust digital assistant that could do many things, and integrate with many services—even though it was being built by a startup with limited funds and people. After Apple bought Siri, the giant company seemed to treat it as a backwater, restricting it to doing only a few, slowly increasing number of tasks, like telling you the weather, sports scores, movie and restaurant listings, and controlling the device's functions. Its unhappy founders have left Apple to build a new AI service called <a href="/wiki/Viv_(software)" title="Viv (software)">Viv</a>. And, on too many occasions, Siri either gets things wrong, doesn't know the answer, or can't verbalize it. Instead, it shows you a web search result, even when you're not in a position to read it.</p></blockquote>
<p>In October 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a></i> reported that Apple had plans to unify the teams behind its various cloud-based services, including a single campus and reorganized cloud computing resources aimed at improving the processing of Siri's queries,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although another report from <i>The Verge</i>, in June 2017, once again called Siri's voice recognition "bad."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> published an extensive report on the lack of innovation with Siri following competitors' advancement in the field of voice assistants. Noting that Apple workers' anxiety levels "went up a notch" on the announcement of Amazon's Alexa, the <i>Journal</i> wrote: "Today, Apple is playing catch-up in a product category it invented, increasing worries about whether the technology giant has lost some of its innovation edge." The report gave the primary causes being Apple's prioritization of user privacy, including randomly-tagged six-month Siri searches, whereas Google and Amazon keep data until actively discarded by the user,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2022)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and executive power struggles within Apple. Apple did not comment on the report, while <a href="/wiki/Eddy_Cue" title="Eddy Cue">Eddy Cue</a> said: "Apple often uses generic data rather than user data to train its systems and has the ability to improve Siri's performance for individual users with information kept on their iPhones."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WSJ&#95;innovation&#95;15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_innovation-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Privacy_controversy">Privacy controversy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Privacy controversy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In July 2019, a then-anonymous whistleblower and former Apple contractor Thomas le Bonniec said that Siri regularly records some of its users' conversations when activated, which often happened unintentionally. The recordings are sent to Apple contractors grading Siri's responses on a variety of factors. Among other things, the contractors regularly hear private conversations between doctors and patients, business and drug deals, and couples having sex. Apple did not disclose this in its privacy documentation and did not provide a way for its users to opt-in or out.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:How_legendary_is_siri%3F.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/How_legendary_is_siri%3F.png/250px-How_legendary_is_siri%3F.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/How_legendary_is_siri%3F.png/500px-How_legendary_is_siri%3F.png 1.5x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="408" /></a><figcaption>An example of a conversation with Siri</figcaption></figure>
<p>In August 2019, Apple apologized, halted the Siri grading program, and said that it plans to resume "later this fall when software updates are released to [its] users".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company also announced "it would no longer listen to Siri recordings without your permission".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> iOS 13.2, released in October 2019, introduced the ability to opt out of the grading program and to delete all the voice recordings that Apple has stored on its servers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users were given the choice of whether their audio data was received by Apple or not, with the ability to change their decision as often as they like. It was then made an opt-in program.
</p><p>In May 2020, Thomas le Bonniec revealed himself as the whistleblower and sent a letter to European data protection regulators, calling on them to investigate Apple's "past and present" use of Siri recordings. He argued that, even though Apple has apologized, it has never faced the consequences for its years-long grading program.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2024, Apple agreed to a $95 million class-action settlement, compensating users of Siri-enabled from the past ten years. Additionally, Apple must confirm the deletion of Siri recordings before 2019 (when the feature became opt-in) and issue new guidance on how data is collected and how users can participate in efforts to improve Siri.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Social_impacts_and_awareness">Social impacts and awareness</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Social impacts and awareness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Disability">Disability</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Disability"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Apple has introduced various accessibility features aimed at making its devices more inclusive for individuals with disabilities. The company provides users the opportunity to share feedback on accessibility features through email.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some of the new functionalities include live speech, personal voice, Siri's atypical speech pattern recognition, and much more.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Accessibility features:
</p>
<ul><li>VoiceOver: This feature provides visual feedback for Siri responses, allowing users to engage with Siri through both visual and auditory channels.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Voice-to-text and text-to-voice: Siri can transcribe spoken words into and text as well as read text typed by the user out loud.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Text commands: Users can type what they want Siri to do.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Personal voice: This allows users to create a synthesized voice that sounds like them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bias">Bias</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Bias"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Siri, like many AI systems, can perpetuate gender and racial biases through its design and functionality. As argued by <i>The Conversation</i>, Siri "reinforces the role of women as secondary and submissive to men" due to the fact that the default is a soft, female voice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to an article from <i>The Scientific American</i>, Claudia Lloreda explains that non-native English speakers have to "adapt our way of speaking to interact with speech-recognition technologies."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Furthermore, due to repetitive "learnings" from a larger user base, Siri may unintentionally produce a Western perspective, limiting representation and furthering biases in everyday interactions. Despite these perpetuated issues, Siri does provide several benefits as well, especially for those with disabilities that typically limit their abilities to use technology and access the internet. Apple has since introduced a larger variety of voices with different accents and languages.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Swearing">Swearing</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Swearing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The iOS version of Siri ships with a vulgar content filter; however, it is disabled by default and must be enabled by the user manually.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a></i> reported a new glitch that could be exploited by a user requesting the definition of "<a href="/wiki/Mother" title="Mother">mother</a>" be read out loud. Siri would issue a response and ask the user if they would like to hear the next definition; when the user replies with "yes", Siri would mention "mother" as being short for "<a href="/wiki/Motherfucker" title="Motherfucker">motherfucker</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This resulted in multiple <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> videos featuring the responses or how to trigger them, or both. Apple fixed the issue silently. The content is picked up from third-party sources such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> and not a supplied message from the corporation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: In popular culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Siri provided the voice of <a href="/wiki/Batcomputer" class="mw-redirect" title="Batcomputer">'Puter</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lego_Batman_Movie" title="The Lego Batman Movie">The Lego Batman Movie</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
